10066{_}1869{_}The other made no reply; a weight seemed to have fallen upon him along with his new outfit, and he slunk into the darkness.
10066{_}1870{_}George made a move to follow; there was a muffled shriek from Godwin, who fled headlong; and then a sharp command from Donnegan stopped the big man.
10066{_}1871{_}"Come here," said Donnegan.
10066{_}1872{_}George Washington Green rode slowly closer.
10066{_}1873{_}"If I let you go what would you do?"
10066{_}1874{_}There was a glint of teeth.
10066{_}1875{_}"I'd find him."
10066{_}1876{_}"And break him in two, eh?
10066{_}1877{_}Instead, I'm going to take you home, where you'll have a chance of breaking me in two instead.
10066{_}1878{_}There's something about the cut of your shoulders and your head that I like, Green; and if you don't murder me in the first hour or so, I think we'll get on very well together.
10066{_}1879{_}You hear?"
10066{_}1880{_}The silence of George Washington Green was a tremendous thing.
10066{_}1881{_}"Now ride ahead of me.
10066{_}1882{_}I'll direct you how to go."
10066{_}1883{_}He went first straight back through the town and up the hill to the two tents.
10066{_}1884{_}He made George go before him into the tent and take up the roll of bedding; and then, with George and the bedding leading the way, and Donnegan leading the two horses behind, they went across the hillside to a shack which he had seen vacated that evening.
10066{_}1885{_}It certainly could not be rented again before morning, and in the meantime Donnegan would be in possession, which was a large part of the law in The Corner, as he knew.
10066{_}1886{_}A little lean-to against the main shack served as a stable; the creek down the hillside was the watering trough.
10066{_}1887{_}And Donnegan stood by while the big Negro silently tended to the horses--removing the packs and preparing them for the night.
10066{_}1888{_}Still in silence he produced a small lantern and lighted it.
10066{_}1889{_}It showed his face for the first time--the skin ebony black and polished over the cheekbones, but the rest of the face almost handsome, except that the slight flare of his nostrils gave him a cast of inhuman ferocity.
10066{_}1890{_}And the fierceness was given point by a pair of arms of gorilla length; broad shoulders padded with rolling muscles, and the neck of a bull.
10066{_}1891{_}On the whole, Donnegan, a connoisseur of fighting men, had never seen such promise of strength.
10066{_}1892{_}At his gesture, George led the way into the house.
10066{_}1893{_}It was more commodious than most of the shacks of The Corner.
10066{_}1894{_}In place of a single room this had two compartments--one for the kitchen and another for the living room.
10066{_}1895{_}In vacating the hut, the last occupants had left some of the furnishings behind them.
10066{_}1896{_}There was a mirror, for instance, in the corner; and beneath the mirror a cheap table in whose open drawer appeared a tumble of papers.
10066{_}1897{_}Donnegan dropped the heavy sack of Godwin's winnings to the floor, and while George hung the lantern on a nail on the wall, Donnegan crossed to the table and appeared to run through the papers.
10066{_}1898{_}He was humming carelessly while he did it, but all the time he watched with catlike intensity the reflection of George in the mirror above him.
10066{_}1899{_}He saw--rather dimly, for the cheap glass showed all its images in waves--that George turned abruptly after hanging up the lantern, paused, and then whipped a hand into his coat pocket and out again.
10066{_}1900{_}Donnegan leaped lightly to one side, and the knife, hissing past his head, buried itself in the wall, and its vibrations set up a vicious humming.
10066{_}1901{_}As for Donnegan, the leap that carried him to one side whirled him about also; he faced the big man, who was now crouched in the very act of following the knife cast with the lunge of his powerful body.
10066{_}1902{_}There was no weapon in Donnegan's hand, and yet George hesitated, balanced--and then slowly drew himself erect.
10066{_}1903{_}He was puzzled.
10066{_}1904{_}An outburst of oaths, the flash of a gun, and he would have been at home in the brawl, but the silence, the smile of Donnegan and the steady glance were too much for him.
10066{_}1905{_}He moistened his lips, and yet he could not speak.
10066{_}1906{_}And Donnegan knew that what paralyzed George was the manner in which he had received warning.
10066{_}1907{_}Evidently the simple explanation of the mirror did not occur to the fellow; and the whole incident took on supernatural colorings.
10066{_}1908{_}A phrase of explanation and Donnegan would become again an ordinary human being; but while the small link was a mystery the brain and body of George were numb.
10066{_}1909{_}It was necessary above all to continue inexplicable.
10066{_}1910{_}Donnegan, turning, drew the knife from the wall with a jerk.
10066{_}1911{_}Half the length of the keen blade had sunk into the wood--a mute tribute to the force and speed of George's hand--and now Donnegan took the bright little weapon by the point and gave it back to the other.
10066{_}1912{_}"If you throw for the body instead of the head," said Donnegan, "you have a better chance of sending the point home."
10066{_}1913{_}He turned his back again upon the gaping giant, and drawing up a broken box before the open door he sat down to contemplate the night.
10066{_}1914{_}Not a sound behind him.
10066{_}1915{_}It might be that the big fellow had regained his nerve and was stealing up for a second attempt; but Donnegan would have wagered his soul that George Washington Green had his first and last lesson and that he would rather play with bare lightning than ever again cross his new master.
10066{_}1916{_}At length: "When you make down the bunks," said Donnegan, "put mine farthest from the kitchen.
10066{_}1917{_}You had better do that first."
10066{_}1918{_}"Yes--sir," came the deep bass murmur behind him.
10066{_}1919{_}And the heart of Donnegan stirred, for that "sir" meant many things.
10066{_}1920{_}Presently George crossed the floor with a burden; there was the "whish" of the blankets being unrolled--and then a slight pause.
10066{_}1921{_}It seemed to him that he could hear a heavier breathing.
10066{_}1922{_}Why?
10066{_}1923{_}And searching swiftly back through his memory he recalled that his other gun, a stub-nosed thirty-eight, was in the center of his blanket roll.
10066{_}1924{_}And he knew that George had the weapon in his big hand.
10066{_}1925{_}One pressure of the trigger would put an end to Donnegan; one bullet would give George the canvas sack and its small treasure.
10066{_}1926{_}"When you clean my gun," said Donnegan, "take the action to pieces and go over every part."
10066{_}1927{_}He could actually feel the start of George.
10066{_}1928{_}Then: "Yes, sir," in a subdued whisper.
10066{_}1929{_}If the escape from the knife had startled George, this second incident had convinced him that his new master possessed eyes in the back of his head.
10066{_}1930{_}And Donnegan, paying no further heed to him, looked steadily across the hillside to the white tent of Lou Macon, fifty yards away.
10066{_}1931{_}16   His plan, grown to full stature so swiftly, and springing out of nothing, well nigh, had come out of his first determination to bring Jack Landis back to Lou Macon; for he could interpret those blank, misty eyes with which she had sat after the departure of Landis in only one way.
10066{_}1932{_}Yet to rule even the hand of big Jack Landis would be hard enough and to rule his heart was quite another story.
10066{_}1933{_}Remembering Nelly Lebrun, he saw clearly that the only way in which he could be brought back to Lou was first to remove Nelly as a possibility in his eyes.
10066{_}1934{_}But how remove Nelly as long as it was her cue from her father to play Landis for his money?
10066{_}1935{_}How remove her, unless it were possible to sweep Nelly off her feet with another man?
10066{_}1936{_}She might, indeed, be taken by storm, and if she once slighted Landis for the sake of another, his boyish pride would probably do the rest, and his next step would be to return to Lou Macon.
10066{_}1937{_}All this seemed logical, but where find the man to storm the heart of Nelly and dazzle her bright, clever eyes?
10066{_}1938{_}His own rags had made him shrug his shoulders; and it was the thought of clothes which had made him fasten his attention so closely on the man of the linen suit in Lebrun's.
10066{_}1939{_}Donnegan with money, with well-fitted clothes, and with a few notorious escapades behind him--yes, Donnegan with such a flying start might flutter the heart of Nelly Lebrun for a moment.
10066{_}1940{_}But he must have the money, the clothes, and then he must deliberately set out to startle The Corner, make himself a public figure, talked of, pointed at, known, feared, respected, and even loved by at least a few.
10066{_}1941{_}He must accomplish all these things beginning at a literal zero.
10066{_}1942{_}It was the impossible nature of this that tempted Donnegan.
10066{_}1943{_}But the paradoxical picture of the ragged skulker in Milligan's actually sitting at the same table with Nelly Lebrun and receiving her smiles stayed with him.
10066{_}1944{_}He intended to rise, literally Phoenixlike, out of ashes.
10066{_}1945{_}And the next morning, in the red time of the dawn, he sat drinking the coffee which George Washington Green had made for him and considering the details of the problem.
10066{_}1946{_}Clothes, which had been a main obstacle, were now accounted for, since, as he had suspected, the packs of Godwin contained a luxurious wardrobe of considerable compass.
10066{_}1947{_}At that moment, for instance, Donnegan was wrapped in a dressing gown of padded silk and his feet were encased in slippers.
10066{_}1948{_}But clothes were the least part of his worries.
10066{_}1949{_}To startle The Corner, and thereby make himself attractive in the eyes of Nelly Lebrun, overshadowing Jack Landis--that was the thing!
10066{_}1950{_}But to startle The Corner, where gold strikes were events of every twenty-four hours, just now--where robberies were common gossip, and where the killings now averaged nearly three a day--to startle The Corner was like trying to startle the theatrical world with a sensational play.
10066{_}1951{_}Indeed, this parallel could have been pursued, for Donnegan was the nameless actor and the mountain desert was the stage on which he intended to become a headliner.
10066{_}1952{_}No wonder, then, that his lean face was compressed in thought.
10066{_}1953{_}Yet no one could have guessed it by his conversation.
10066{_}1954{_}At the moment he was interrupted, his talk ran somewhat as follows.
10066{_}1955{_}"George, Godwin taught you how to make coffee?"
10066{_}1956{_}"Yes, sir," from George.
10066{_}1957{_}Since the night before he had appeared totally subdued.
10066{_}1958{_}Never once did he venture a comment.
10066{_}1959{_}And ever Donnegan was conscious of big, bright eyes watching him in a reverent fear not untinged by superstition.
10066{_}1960{_}Once, in the middle of the night, he had wakened and seen the vast shadow of George's form leaning over the sack of money.
10066{_}1961{_}Murder by stealth in the dark had been in the giant's mind, no doubt.
10066{_}1962{_}But when, after that, he came and leaned over Donnegan's bunk, the master closed his eyes and kept on breathing regularly, and finally George returned to his own place--softly as a gigantic cat.
10066{_}1963{_}Even in the master's sleep he found something to be dreaded, and Donnegan knew that he could now trust the fellow through anything.
10066{_}1964{_}In the morning, at the first touch of light, he had gone to the stores and collected provisions.
10066{_}1965{_}And a comfortable breakfast followed.
10066{_}1966{_}"Godwin," resumed Donnegan, "was talented in many ways."
10066{_}1967{_}The big man showed his teeth in silence; for since Godwin proposed the sacrifice of the servant to preserve himself, George had apparently altered his opinion of the gambler.
10066{_}1968{_}"A talented man, George, but he knew nothing about coffee.
10066{_}1969{_}It should never boil.
10066{_}1970{_}It should only begin to cream through the crust.
10066{_}1971{_}Let that happen; take the pot from the fire; put it back and let the surface cream again.
10066{_}1972{_}Do this three times, and then pour the liquid from the grounds and you have the right strength and the right heating.
10066{_}1973{_}You understand?"
10066{_}1974{_}"Yes, sir."
10066{_}1975{_}"And concerning the frying of bacon--"  At this point the interruption came in the shape of four men at the open door; and one of these Donnegan recognized as the real estate dealer, who had shrewdly set up tents and shacks on every favorable spot in The Corner and was now reaping a rich harvest.
10066{_}1976{_}Gloster was his name.
10066{_}1977{_}It was patent that he did not see in the man in the silk dressing robe the unshaven miscreant of the day before who had rented the two tents.
10066{_}1978{_}"How'dee," he said, standing on the threshold, with the other three in the background.
10066{_}1979{_}Donnegan looked at him and through him.
10066{_}1980{_}"My name is Gloster.
10066{_}1981{_}I own this shack and I've come to find out why you're in it."
10066{_}1982{_}"George," said Donnegan, "speak to him.
10066{_}1983{_}Tel!
10066{_}1984{_}him that I know houses are scarce in The Corner; that I found this place by accident vacant; that I intend to stay in it on purpose."
10066{_}1985{_}George Washington Green instantly rose to the situation; he swallowed a vast grin and strode to the door.
10066{_}1986{_}And though Mr. Gloster's face crimsoned with rage at such treatment he controlled his voice.
10066{_}1987{_}In The Corner manhood was apt to be reckoned by the pound, and George was a giant.
10066{_}1988{_}"I heard what your boss said, buddie," said Gloster.
10066{_}1989{_}"But I've rented this cabin and the next one to these three gents and their party, and they want a home.
10066{_}1990{_}Nothing to do but vacate.
10066{_}1991{_}Which speed is the thing I want.
10066{_}1992{_}Thirty minutes will--"  "Thirty minutes don't change nothing," declared George in his deep, soft voice.
10066{_}1993{_}The real estate man choked.
10066{_}1994{_}Then: "You tell your boss that jumping a cabin is like jumping a claim.
10066{_}1995{_}They's a law in The Corner for gents like him."
10066{_}1996{_}George made a gesture of helplessness; but Gloster turned to the three.
10066{_}1997{_}"Both shacks or none at all," said the spokesman.
10066{_}1998{_}"One ain't big enough to do us any good.
10066{_}1999{_}But if this bird won't vamoose--"  He was a tolerably rough-appearing sort and he was backed by two of a kind.
10066{_}2000{_}No doubt dangerous action would have followed had not George shown himself capable of rising to a height.
10066{_}2001{_}He stepped from the door; he approached Gloster and said in a confidential whisper that reached easily to the other three: "They ain't any call for a quick play, mister.
10066{_}2002{_}Watch yo'selves.
10066{_}2003{_}Maybe you don't know who the boss is?"
10066{_}2004{_}"And what's more, I don't care," said Gloster defiantly but with his voice instinctively lowered.
10066{_}2005{_}He stared past George, and behold, the man in the dressing gown still sat in quiet and sipped his coffee.
10066{_}2006{_}"It's Donnegan," whispered George.
10066{_}2007{_}"Don--who's he?"
10066{_}2008{_}"You don't know Donnegan?"
10066{_}2009{_}The mingled contempt and astonishment of George would have moved a thing of stone.
10066{_}2010{_}It certainly troubled Gloster.
10066{_}2011{_}And he turned to the three.
10066{_}2012{_}"Gents," he said, "they's two things we can do.
10066{_}2013{_}Try the law--and law's a lame lady in these parts--or throw him out.
10066{_}2014{_}Say which?"
10066{_}2015{_}The three looked from Gloster to the shack; from the shack to Donnegan, absently sipping his coffee; from Donnegan to George, who stood exhibiting a broad grin of anticipated delight.
10066{_}2016{_}The contrast was too much for them.
10066{_}2017{_}There is one great and deep-seated terror in the mountain desert, and that is for the man who may be other than he seems.
10066{_}2018{_}The giant with the rough voice and the boisterous ways is generally due for a stormy passage west of the Rockies; but the silent man with the gentle manners receives respect.
10066{_}2019{_}Traditions live of desperadoes with exteriors of womanish calm and the action of devils.
10066{_}2020{_}And Donnegan sipping his morning coffee fitted into the picture which rumor had painted.
10066{_}2021{_}The three looked at one another, declared that they had not come to fight for a house but to rent one, that the real estate agent could go to the devil for all of them, and that they were bound elsewhere.
10066{_}2022{_}So they departed and left Gloster both relieved and gloomy.
10066{_}2023{_}"Now," said Donnegan to George, "tell him that we'll take both the shacks, and he can add fifty per cent to his old price."
10066{_}2024{_}The bargain was concluded on the spot; the money was paid by George.
10066{_}2025{_}Gloster went down the hill to tell The Corner that a mystery had hit the town and George brought the canvas bag back to Donnegan with the top still untied--as though to let it be seen that he had not pocketed any of the gold.
10066{_}2026{_}"I don't want to count it," said Donnegan.
10066{_}2027{_}"Keep the bag, George.
10066{_}2028{_}Keep money in your pocket.
10066{_}2029{_}Treat both of us well.
10066{_}2030{_}And when that's gone I'll get more."
10066{_}2031{_}If the manner in which Donnegan had handled the renting of the cabins had charmed George, he was wholly entranced by this last touch of free spending.
10066{_}2032{_}To serve a man who was his master was one thing; to serve one who trusted him so completely was quite another.
10066{_}2033{_}To live under the same roof with a man who was a riddle was sufficiently delightful; but to be allowed actually to share in the mystery was a superhappiness.
10066{_}2034{_}He was singing when he started to wash the dishes, and Donnegan went across the hill to the tent of Lou Macon.
10066{_}2035{_}She was laying the fire before the tent; and the morning freshness had cleared from her face any vestige of the trouble of the night before; and in the slant light her hair was glorious, all ruffling gold, semitransparent.
10066{_}2036{_}She did not smile at him; but she could give the effect of smiling while her face remained grave; it was her inward calm content of which people were aware.
10066{_}2037{_}"You missed me?"
10066{_}2038{_}"Yes."
10066{_}2039{_}"You were worried?"
10066{_}2040{_}"No."
10066{_}2041{_}He felt himself put quietly at a distance.
10066{_}2042{_}So he took her up the hill to her new home--the shack beside his own; and George cooked her breakfast.
10066{_}2043{_}When she had been served, Donnegan drew the big man to one side.
10066{_}2044{_}"She's your mistress," said Donnegan.
10066{_}2045{_}"Everything you do for her is worth two things you do for me.
10066{_}2046{_}Watch her as if she were in your eye.
10066{_}2047{_}And if a hair of her head is ever harmed--you see that fire burning yonder--the bed of coals?"
10066{_}2048{_}"Sir?"
10066{_}2049{_}"I'll catch you and make a fire like that and feed you into it--by inches!"
10066{_}2050{_}And the pale face of Donnegan became for an instant the face of a demon.
10066{_}2051{_}George Washington Green saw, and never forgot.
10066{_}2052{_}Afterward, in order that he might think, Donnegan got on one of the horses he had taken from Godwin and rode over the hills.
10066{_}2053{_}They were both leggy chestnuts, with surprising signs of blood' and all the earmarks of sprinters; but in Godwin's trade sharp getaways were probably often necessary.
10066{_}2054{_}The pleasure he took in the action of the animal kept him from getting into his problem.
10066{_}2055{_}How to startle The Corner?
10066{_}2056{_}How follow up the opening gun which he had fired at the expense of Gloster and the three miners?
10066{_}2057{_}He broke off, later in the day, to write a letter to Colonel Macon, informing him that Jack Landis was tied hard and fast by Nelly Lebrun and that for the present nothing could be done except wait, unless the colonel had suggestions to offer.
10066{_}2058{_}The thought of the colonel, however, stimulated Donnegan.
10066{_}2059{_}And before midafternoon he had thought of a thing to do.
10066{_}2060{_}17   The bar in Milligan's was not nearly so pretentious an affair as the bar in Lebrun's, but it was of a far higher class.
10066{_}2061{_}Milligan had even managed to bring in a few bottles of wine, and he had dispensed cheap claret at two dollars a glass when the miners wished to celebrate a rare occasion.
10066{_}2062{_}There were complaints, not of the taste, but of the lack of strength.
10066{_}2063{_}So Milligan fortified his liquor with pure alcohol and after that the claret went like a sweet song in The Corner.
10066{_}2064{_}Among other things, he sold mint juleps; and it was the memory of the big sign proclaiming this fact that furnished Donnegan with his idea.
10066{_}2065{_}He had George Washington Green put on his town clothes--a riding suit in which Godwin had had him dress for the sake of formal occasions.
10066{_}2066{_}Resplendent in black boots, yellow riding breeches, and blue silk shirt, the big man came before Donnegan for instructions.
10066{_}2067{_}"Go down to Milligan's," said the master.
10066{_}2068{_}"They don't allow colored people to enter the door, but you go to the door and start for the bar.
10066{_}2069{_}They won't let you go very far.
10066{_}2070{_}When they stop you, tell them you come from Donnegan and that you have to get me some mint for a julep.
10066{_}2071{_}Insist.
10066{_}2072{_}The bouncer will start to throw you out."
10066{_}2073{_}George showed his teeth.
10066{_}2074{_}"No fighting back.
10066{_}2075{_}Don't lift your hand.
10066{_}2076{_}When you find that you can't get in, come back here.
10066{_}2077{_}Now, ride."
10066{_}2078{_}So George mounted the horse and went.
10066{_}2079{_}Straight to Milligan's he rode and dismounted; and half of The Corner's scant daytime population came into the street to see the brilliant horseman pass.
10066{_}2080{_}Scar-faced Lewis met the big man at the door.
10066{_}2081{_}And size meant little to Andy, except an easier target.
10066{_}2082{_}"Well, confound my soul," said Lewis, blocking the way.
10066{_}2083{_}"A Negro in Milligan's?
10066{_}2084{_}Get out!"
10066{_}2085{_}Big George did not move.
10066{_}2086{_}"I been sent, mister," he said mildly.
10066{_}2087{_}"I been sent for enough mint to make a julep."
10066{_}2088{_}"You been sent to the wrong place," declared Andy, hitching at his cartridge belt.
10066{_}2089{_}"Ain't you seen that sign?"
10066{_}2090{_}And he pointed to the one which eliminated colored patrons.
10066{_}2091{_}"Signs don't mean nothin' to my boss," said George.
10066{_}2092{_}"Who's he?"
10066{_}2093{_}"Donnegan."
10066{_}2094{_}"And who's Donnegan?"
10066{_}2095{_}It puzzled George.
10066{_}2096{_}He scratched his head in bewilderment seeking for an explanation.
10066{_}2097{_}"Donnegan is--Donnegan," he explained.
10066{_}2098{_}"I heard Gloster talk about him," offered someone in the rapidly growing group.
10066{_}2099{_}"He's the gent that rented the two places on the hill."
10066{_}2100{_}"Tell him to come himse'f," said Andy Lewis.
10066{_}2101{_}"We don't play no favorites at Milligan's."
10066{_}2102{_}"Mister," said big George, "I don't want to bring no trouble on this heah place, but--don't make me go back and bring Donnegan."
10066{_}2103{_}Even Andy Lewis was staggered by this assurance.
10066{_}2104{_}"Rules is rules," he finally decided.
10066{_}2105{_}"And out you go."
10066{_}2106{_}Big George stepped from the doorway and mounted his horse.
10066{_}2107{_}"I call on all you gen'lemen," he said to the assembled group, "to say that I done tried my best to do this peaceable.
10066{_}2108{_}It ain't me that's sent for Donnegan; it's him!"
10066{_}2109{_}He rode away, leaving Scar-faced Lewis biting his long mustaches in anxiety.
10066{_}2110{_}He was not exactly afraid, but he waited in the suspense which comes before a battle.
10066{_}2111{_}Moreover, an audience was gathering.
10066{_}2112{_}The word went about as only a rumor of mischief can travel.
10066{_}2113{_}New men had gathered.
10066{_}2114{_}The few day gamblers tumbled out of Lebrun's across the street to watch the fun.
10066{_}2115{_}The storekeepers were in their doors.
10066{_}2116{_}Lebrun himself, withered and dark and yellow of eye, came to watch.
10066{_}2117{_}And here and there through the crowd there was a spot of color where the women of the town appeared.
10066{_}2118{_}And among others, Nelly Lebrun with Jack Landis beside her.
10066{_}2119{_}On the whole it was not a large crowd, but what it lacked in size it made up in intense interest.
10066{_}2120{_}For though The Corner had had its share of troubles of fist and gun, most of them were entirely impromptu affairs.
10066{_}2121{_}Here was a fight in the offing for which the stage was set, the actors set in full view of a conveniently posted audience, and all the suspense of a curtain rising.
10066{_}2122{_}The waiting bore in upon Andy Lewis.
10066{_}2123{_}Without a doubt he intended to kill his man neatly and with dispatch, but the possibility of missing before such a crowd as this sent a chill up and down his spine.
10066{_}2124{_}If he failed now his name would be a sign for laughter ever after in The Corner.
10066{_}2125{_}A hum passed down the street; it rose to a chuckle, and then fell away to sudden silence, for Donnegan was coming.
10066{_}2126{_}He came on a prancing chestnut horse which sidled uneasily on a weaving course, as though it wished to show off for the benefit of the rider and the crowd at once.
10066{_}2127{_}It was a hot afternoon and Donnegan's linen riding suit shone an immaculate white.
10066{_}2128{_}He came straight down the street, as unaware of the audience which awaited him as though he rode in a park where crowds were the common thing.
10066{_}2129{_}Behind him came George Green, just a careful length back.
10066{_}2130{_}Rumor went before the two with a whisper on either side.
10066{_}2131{_}"That's Donnegan.
10066{_}2132{_}There he comes!"
10066{_}2133{_}"Who's Donnegan?"
10066{_}2134{_}"Gloster's man.
10066{_}2135{_}The one who bluffed out Gloster and three others."
10066{_}2136{_}"He pulled his shooting iron and trimmed the whiskers of one of 'em with a chunk of lead."
10066{_}2137{_}"D'you mean that?"
10066{_}2138{_}"What's that kind of a gent doing in The Corner?"
10066{_}2139{_}"Come to buy, I guess.
10066{_}2140{_}He looks like money."
10066{_}2141{_}"Looks like a confounded dude."
10066{_}2142{_}"We'll see his hand in a minute."
10066{_}2143{_}Donnegan was now opposite the dance hall, and Andy Lewis had his hand touching the butt of his gun, but though Donnegan was looking straight at him, he kept his reins in one hand and his heavy riding crop in the other.
10066{_}2144{_}And without a move toward his own gun, he rode straight up to the door of the dance hall, with Andy in front of it.
10066{_}2145{_}George drew rein behind him and turned upon the crowd one broad, superior grin.
10066{_}2146{_}As who should say: "I promised you lightning; now watch it strike!"
10066{_}2147{_}If the crowd had been expectant before, it was now reduced to wire-drawn tenseness.
10066{_}2148{_}"Are you the fellow who turned back my man?"
10066{_}2149{_}asked Donnegan.
10066{_}2150{_}His quiet voice fell coldly upon the soul of Andy.
10066{_}2151{_}He strove to warm himself by an outbreak of temper.
10066{_}2152{_}"They ain't any poor fool dude can call me a fellow!"
10066{_}2153{_}he shouted.
10066{_}2154{_}The crowd blinked; but when it opened its eyes the gunplay had not occurred.
10066{_}2155{_}The hand of Andy was relaxing from the butt of his gun and an expression of astonishment and contempt was growing upon his face.
10066{_}2156{_}"I haven't come to curse you," said the rider, still occupying his hands with crop and reins.
10066{_}2157{_}"I've come to ask you a question and get an answer.
10066{_}2158{_}Are you the fellow who turned back my man?"
10066{_}2159{_}"I guess you ain't the kind I was expectin' to call on me," drawled Andy, his fear gone, and he winked at the crowd.
10066{_}2160{_}But the others were not yet ready to laugh.
10066{_}2161{_}Something about the calm face of Donnegan had impressed them.
10066{_}2162{_}"Sure, I'm the one that kicked him out.
10066{_}2163{_}He ain't allowed in there."
10066{_}2164{_}"It's the last of my thoughts to break in upon a convention in your city," replied the grave rider, "but my man was sent on an errand and therefore he had a right to expect courtesy.
10066{_}2165{_}George, get off your horse and go into Milligan's place.
10066{_}2166{_}I want that mint!"
10066{_}2167{_}For a moment Andy was too stunned to answer.
10066{_}2168{_}Then his voice came harshly and he swayed from side to side, gathering and summoning his wrath.
10066{_}2169{_}"Keep out boy!
10066{_}2170{_}Keep out, or you're buzzard meat.
10066{_}2171{_}I'm warnin'--"  For the first time his glance left the rider to find George, and that instant was fatal.
10066{_}2172{_}The hand of Donnegan licked out as the snake's tongue darts--the loaded quirt slipped over in his hand, and holding it by the lash he brought the butt of it thudding on the head of Andy.
10066{_}2173{_}Even then the instinct to fight remained in the stunned man; while he fell, he was drawing the revolver; he lay in a crumpling heap at the feet of Donnegan's horse with the revolver shoved muzzle first into the sand.
10066{_}2174{_}Donnegan's voice did not rise.
10066{_}2175{_}"Go in and get that mint, George," he ordered.
10066{_}2176{_}"And hurry.
10066{_}2177{_}This rascal has kept me waiting until I'm thirsty."
10066{_}2178{_}Big George hesitated only one instant--it was to sweep the crowd for the second time with his confident grin--and he strode through the door of the dance hall.
10066{_}2179{_}As for Donnegan, his only movement was to swing his horse around and shift riding crop and reins into the grip of his left hand.
10066{_}2180{_}His other hand was dropped carelessly upon his hip.
10066{_}2181{_}Now, both these things were very simple maneuvers, but The Corner noted that his change of face had enabled Donnegan to bring the crowd under his eye, and that his right hand was now ready for a more serious bit of work if need be.
10066{_}2182{_}Moreover, he was probing faces with his glance.
10066{_}2183{_}And every armed man in that group felt that the eye of the rider was directed particularly toward him.
10066{_}2184{_}There had been one brief murmur; then the silence lay heavily again, for it was seen that Andy had been only slightly stunned--knocked out, as a boxer might be.
10066{_}2185{_}Now his sturdy brains were clearing.
10066{_}2186{_}His body stiffened into a human semblance once more; he fumbled, found the butt of his gun with his first move.
10066{_}2187{_}He pushed his hat straight: and so doing he raked the welt which the blow had left on his head.
10066{_}2188{_}The pain finished clearing the mist from his mind; in an instant he was on his feet, maddened with shame.
10066{_}2189{_}He saw the semicircle of white faces, and the whole episode flashed back on him.
10066{_}2190{_}He had been knocked down like a dog.
10066{_}2191{_}For a moment he looked into the blank faces of the crowd; someone noted that there was no gun strapped at the side of Donnegan.
10066{_}2192{_}A voice shouted a warning.
10066{_}2193{_}"Stop, Lewis.
10066{_}2194{_}The dude ain't got a gun.
10066{_}2195{_}It's murder!"
10066{_}2196{_}It was now that Lewis saw Donnegan sitting the saddle directly behind him, and he whirled with a moan of fury.
10066{_}2197{_}It was a twist of his body--in his eagerness--rather than a turning upon his feet.
10066{_}2198{_}And he was half around before the rider moved.
10066{_}2199{_}Then he conjured a gun from somewhere in his clothes.
10066{_}2200{_}There was the flash of the steel, an explosion, and Scar-faced Lewis was on his knees with a scream of pain holding his right forearm with his left hand.
10066{_}2201{_}The crowd hesitated still for a second, as though it feared to interfere; but Donnegan had already put up his weapon.
10066{_}2202{_}A wave of the curious spectators rushed across the street and gathered around the injured man.
10066{_}2203{_}They found that he had been shot through the fleshy part of the thumb, and the bullet, ranging down the arm, had sliced a furrow to the bone all the way to the elbow.
10066{_}2204{_}It was a grisly wound.
10066{_}2205{_}Big George Washington Green came running to the door of the dance hall with a sprig of something green in his hand; one glance assured him that all was well; and once more that wide, confident grin spread upon his face.
10066{_}2206{_}He came to the master and offered the mint; and Donnegan, raising it to his face, inhaled the scent deeply.
10066{_}2207{_}"Good," he said.
10066{_}2208{_}"And now for a julep, George!
10066{_}2209{_}Let's go home!"
10066{_}2210{_}Across the street a dark-eyed girl had clasped the arm of her companion in hysterical excitement.
10066{_}2211{_}"Did you see?"
10066{_}2212{_}she asked of her tall companion.
10066{_}2213{_}"I saw a murderer shoot down a man; he ought to be hung for it!"
10066{_}2214{_}"But the mint!
10066{_}2215{_}Did you see him smile over it?
10066{_}2216{_}Oh, what a devil he is; and what a man!"
10066{_}2217{_}Jack Landis flashed a glance of suspicion down at her, but her dancing eyes had quite forgotten him.
10066{_}2218{_}They were following the progress of Donnegan down the street.
10066{_}2219{_}He rode slowly, and George kept that formal distance, just a length behind.

10066{_}2221{_}It was a rather helpless milling around the wounded man, and Nelly Lebrun was the one who worked her way through the crowd and came to Andy Lewis.

10066{_}2226{_}The subject was a real one.
10066{_}2227{_}Had Donnegan aimed at the hand of Andy and risked his own life on his ability to disable the other without killing him?

10066{_}2875{_}Of all this Donnegan was fully aware.

10066{_}2905{_}Besides, where such men as Donnegan and big Jack Landis were concerned, there was not apt to be much wild shooting.
10066{_}2906{_}The dancing stopped, of course.
10066{_}2907{_}The music was ordered by Milligan to play, in a frantic endeavor to rouse custom again; but the music of its own accord fell away in the middle of the piece.
10066{_}2908{_}For the musicians could not watch the notes and the door at the same time.
10066{_}2909{_}As for Donnegan, he found that it was one thing to wait and another to be waited for.
10066{_}2910{_}He, too, wished to turn and watch that door until it should be filled by the bulk of Jack Landis.
10066{_}2911{_}Yet he fought the desire.
10066{_}2912{_}And in the midst of this torturing suspense an idea came to him, and at the same instant Jack Landis entered the doorway.
10066{_}2913{_}He stood there looking vast against the night.
10066{_}2914{_}One glance around was sufficient to teach him the meaning of the silence.
10066{_}2915{_}The stage was set, and the way opened to Donnegan.
10066{_}2916{_}Without a word, big George stole to one side.
10066{_}2917{_}Straight to the middle of the dance floor went Jack Landis, red-faced, with long, heavy steps.
10066{_}2918{_}He faced Donnegan.

10066{_}2923{_}Donnegan, too, stirred.

10066{_}2925{_}A terrible chance, for Landis had come within a breath of shooting.

10066{_}3084{_}From the crowd there was a deep breath.

10066{_}3088{_}He made his last play to shatter the nerve of Landis.
10066{_}3089{_}With the minute hand on the very mark, he turned carelessly, the revolver still dangling by the trigger guard, and laughed toward the crowd.

10066{_}3098{_}The blow of the slug, like the punch of a strong man's fist, knocked the victim out of his chair to the floor.

10066{_}3417{_}He had thrown himself upon his bunk and lay face down, his arms stretched rigidly out before him, his teeth set, his eyes closed.
10066{_}3418{_}For what Donnegan had wanted in the world, he had taken; by force when he could, by subtlety when he must.

10066{_}3464{_}Then he left the chair, shaved, and dressed carefully, looked to his revolver, stowed it carefully and invisibly away among his clothes, and walked leisurely down the hill.
10066{_}3465{_}An outbreak of cursing, stamping, hair-tearing, shooting could not have affected big George as this quiet departure did.

10066{_}3469{_}And he went down the hill, making sure that he was fit for battle with knife and gun.
10066{_}3470{_}He had sensed Donnegan's mental condition accurately enough.
10066{_}3471{_}The heart of the little man was swelled to the point of breaking.
10066{_}3472{_}A twenty-hour vigil had whitened his face, drawn in his cheeks, and painted his eyes with shadow; and now he wanted action.
10066{_}3473{_}He wanted excitement, strife, competition; something to fill his mind.
10066{_}3474{_}And naturally enough he had two places in mind--Lebrun's and Milligan's.
10066{_}3475{_}It is hard to relate the state of Donnegan's mind at this time.

10066{_}3482{_}He was only a man, and, since his heart was empty, he wanted something that might fill it.
10066{_}3483{_}Indeed, like most men, suffering made him a good deal of a boy.

10066{_}3487{_}George, at a signal from the master, raked in the winnings.
10066{_}3488{_}And Donnegan sat at a faro table and won again, and again rose disconsolately and went on.
10066{_}3489{_}For when men do not care how luck runs it never fails to favor them.
10066{_}3490{_}The devotees of fortune are the ones she punishes.

10066{_}3492{_}"Donnegan is out hunting trouble."
10066{_}3493{_}About the good that is in men rumor often makes mistakes, but for evil she has an infallible eye and at once sets all of her thousand tongues wagging.
10066{_}3494{_}Indeed, any man with half an eye could not fail to get the meaning of his fixed glance, his hard set jaw, and the straightness of his mouth.

10066{_}3497{_}The true Westerner avoids trouble, but cornered, he will fight like a wildcat.

10066{_}3500{_}There was no competition.

10066{_}4024{_}Nelly Lebrun noted this as she dressed and made up her mind accordingly.

10066{_}4156{_}31   If Nelly Lebrun had consigned him mentally to the worms, that thought made not the slightest impression upon Donnegan.
10066{_}4157{_}A chance for action was opening before him, and above all a chance of action in the eye of Lou Macon; and he welcomed with open arms the thought that he would have an opportunity to strike for her, and keep Landis with her.
10066{_}4158{_}He went arrowy straight and arrowy fast to the cabin on the hill, and he found ample evidence that it had become a center of attention in The Corner.

10066{_}4238{_}So Donnegan judged the quality of fighting men, and, looking into the face of Lord Nick, he knew that he had met his equal at last.

10066{_}4282{_}I have a certain position in these parts.

10066{_}4937{_}35   When Nelly Lebrun raised her head from her hands, Donnegan was a far figure; yet even in the distance she could catch the lilt and easy sway of his body; he rode as he walked, lightly, his feet in the stirrups half taking his weight in a semi-English fashion.
10066{_}4938{_}For a moment she was on the verge of spurring after him, but she kept the rein taut and merely stared until he dipped away among the hills.
10066{_}4939{_}For one thing she was quite assured that she could not overtake that hard rider; and, again, she felt that it was useless to interfere.
10066{_}4940{_}To step between Lord Nick and one of his purposes would have been like stepping before an avalanche and commanding it to halt with a raised hand.
10066{_}4941{_}She watched miserably until even the dust cloud dissolved and the bare, brown hills alone remained before her.
10066{_}4942{_}Then she turned away, and hour after hour let her black jog on.
10066{_}4943{_}To Nelly Lebrun this day was one of those still times which come over the life of a person, and in which they see themselves in relation to the rest of the world clearly.
10066{_}4944{_}It would not be true to say that Nelly loved Donnegan.
10066{_}4945{_}Certainly not as yet, for the familiar figure of Lord Nick filled her imagination.
10066{_}4946{_}But the little man was different.
10066{_}4947{_}Lord Nick commanded respect, admiration, obedience; but there was about Donnegan something which touched her in an intimate and disturbing manner.
10066{_}4948{_}She had felt the will-o'-the-wisp flame which burned in him in his great moments.
10066{_}4949{_}It was possible for her to smile at Donnegan; it was possible even to pity him for his fragility, his touchy pride about his size; to criticize his fondness for taking the center of the stage even in a cheap little mining camp like this and strutting about, the center of all attention.
10066{_}4950{_}Yet there were qualities in him which escaped her, a possibility of metallic hardness, a pitiless fire of purpose.
10066{_}4951{_}To Lord Nick, he was as the bull terrier to the mastiff.
10066{_}4952{_}But above all she could not dislodge the memory of his strange talk with her at Lebrun's.
10066{_}4953{_}Not that she did not season the odd avowals of Donnegan with a grain of salt, but even when she had discounted all that he said, she retained a quivering interest.
10066{_}4954{_}Somewhere beneath his words she sensed reality.
10066{_}4955{_}Somewhere beneath his actions she felt a selfless willingness to throw himself away.
10066{_}4956{_}As she rode she was comparing him steadily with Lord Nick.
10066{_}4957{_}And as she made the comparisons she felt more and more assured that she could pick and choose between the two.
10066{_}4958{_}They loved her, both of them.
10066{_}4959{_}With Nick it was an old story; with Donnegan it might be equally true in spite of its newness.
10066{_}4960{_}And Nelly Lebrun felt rich.
10066{_}4961{_}Not that she would have been willing to give up Lord Nick.
10066{_}4962{_}By no means.
10066{_}4963{_}But neither was she willing to throw away Donnegan.
10066{_}4964{_}Diamonds in one hand and pearls in the other.
10066{_}4965{_}Which handful must she discard?
10066{_}4966{_}She remained riding an unconscionable length of time, and when she drew rein again before her father's house, the black was flecked with foam from his clamped bit, and there was a thick lather under the stirrup leathers.
10066{_}4967{_}She threw the reins to the servant who answered her call and went slowly into the house.
10066{_}4968{_}Donnegan, by this time, was dead.
10066{_}4969{_}She began to feel that it would be hard to look Lord Nick in the face again.
10066{_}4970{_}His other killings had often seemed to her glorious.
10066{_}4971{_}She had rejoiced in the invincibility of her lover.
10066{_}4972{_}Now he suddenly took on the aspect of a murderer.
10066{_}4973{_}She found the house hushed.
10066{_}4974{_}Perhaps everyone was at the gaming house; for now it was midafternoon.
10066{_}4975{_}But when she opened the door to the apartment which they used as a living room she found Joe Rix and the Pedlar and Lester sitting side by side, silent.
10066{_}4976{_}There was no whisky in sight; there were no cards to be seen.
10066{_}4977{_}Marvel of marvels, these three men were spending their time in solemn thought.
10066{_}4978{_}A sudden thought rushed over her, and her cry told where her heart really lay, at least at this time.

10066{_}4980{_}It was Joe Rix who answered.

10066{_}4982{_}"Safe?"
10066{_}4983{_}"Not a scratch."
10066{_}4984{_}She sank into a chair with a sigh, but was instantly on edge again with the second thought.

10066{_}4986{_}she whispered.

10066{_}4988{_}She could not gather the truth of the statement.
10066{_}4989{_}"Then Nick got Landis back before Donnegan returned?"
10066{_}4990{_}"No."
10066{_}4991{_}Like any other girl, Nelly Lebrun hated a puzzle above all things in the world, at least a puzzle which affected her new friends.
10066{_}4992{_}"Lester, what's happened?"
10066{_}4993{_}she demanded.
10066{_}4994{_}At this Lester, who had been brooding upon the floor, raised his eyes and then switched one leg over the other.
10066{_}4995{_}He was a typical cowman, was Lester, from his crimson handkerchief knotted around his throat to his shop-made boots which fitted slenderly about his instep with the care of a gloved hand.

10066{_}5000{_}And briefly he described how Lord Nick had gone up the hill, seen the colonel, come back, taken a horse litter, and gone up the hill again, while the populace of The Corner waited for a crash.
10066{_}5001{_}For Donnegan had arrived in the meantime.
10066{_}5002{_}And how Nick had gone into the cabin, remained a singularly long time, and then come out, with a face half white and half red and an eye that dared anyone to ask questions.

10066{_}5007{_}The girl paid no attention to these remarks.
10066{_}5008{_}She was sunk in a brown study.

10066{_}5014{_}There must have been a showdown of some kind."

10066{_}5042{_}And though his lips parted they closed again before he spoke.

10066{_}5049{_}I know it, don't I?
10066{_}5050{_}And that's why I'm staying here by myself, because the first fool that looks at me with a question in his face, why--I'll break him in two."

10066{_}5061{_}And maybe I'll come over later and join you."
10066{_}5062{_}Seeing Lord Nick before her, so shaken, so gray of face, so dull of eye, she pictured Donnegan as a devil in human form, cunning, resistless.
10066{_}5063{_}"Nick, dear--" she pleaded.
10066{_}5064{_}He closed the door in her face, and she heard his heavy step go back across the room.
10066{_}5065{_}In some mysterious manner she felt the Promethean fire had been stolen from Lord Nick, and Donnegan's was the hand that had robbed him of it.
10066{_}5066{_}36   It was fear that Nelly Lebrun felt first of all.
10066{_}5067{_}It was fear because the impossible had happened and the immovable object had been at last moved.
10066{_}5068{_}Going back to her own room, the record of Lord Nick flashed across her mind; one long series of thrilling deeds.
10066{_}5069{_}He had been a great and widely known figure on the mountain desert while she herself was no more than a girl.
10066{_}5070{_}When she first met him she had been prepared for the sight of a firebreathing monster; and she had never quite recovered from the first thrill of finding him not devil but man.
10066{_}5071{_}Quite oddly, now that there seemed another man as powerful as Lord Nick or even more terrible, she felt for the big man more tenderly than ever; for like all women, there was a corner of her heart into which she wished to receive a thing she could cherish and protect.
10066{_}5072{_}Lord Nick, the invincible, had seemed without any real need of other human beings.
10066{_}5073{_}His love for her had seemed unreal because his need of her seemed a superficial thing.
10066{_}5074{_}Now that he was in sorrow and defeat she suddenly visualized a Lord Nick to whom she could truly be a helpmate.
10066{_}5075{_}Tears came to her eyes at the thought.
10066{_}5076{_}Yet, very contradictorily and very humanly, the moment she was in her room she began preparing her toilet for that evening at Lebrun's.
10066{_}5077{_}Let no one think that she was already preparing to cast Lord Nick away and turn to the new star in the sky of the mountain desert.
10066{_}5078{_}By no means.
10066{_}5079{_}No doubt her own heart was not quite clear to Nelly.
10066{_}5080{_}Indeed, she put on her most lovely gown with a desire for revenge.
10066{_}5081{_}If Lord Nick had been humbled by this singular Donnegan, would it not be a perfect revenge to bring Donnegan himself to her feet?
10066{_}5082{_}Would it not be a joy to see him turn pale under her smile, and then, when he was well-nigh on his knees, spurn the love which he offered her?
10066{_}5083{_}She set her teeth and her eyes gleamed with the thought.
10066{_}5084{_}But nevertheless she went on lavishing care in the preparation for that night.

10066{_}5086{_}In a way she almost regretted that she was admired by such fighting men, Landis, Lord Nick, and now Donnegan, who frightened away the rank and file of other would-be admirers.

10066{_}5226{_}Because, though I have given up hope, I would follow a forlorn chance, a lost cause, and tell you again and again that I love you, Nelly Lebrun!"
10066{_}5227{_}He had half lowered his eyes as he spoke; he had called up a vision, and the face of Lou Macon hovered dimly between him and Nelly Lebrun.
10066{_}5228{_}If all that he spoke was a lie, let him be forgiven for it; it was the golden-haired girl whom he addressed, and it was she who gave the tremor and the fiber to his voice.
10066{_}5229{_}And after all was he not pleading for her happiness as he believed?
10066{_}5230{_}He covered his eyes with his hand; but when he looked up again she could see the shadow of the pain which was slowly passing.
10066{_}5231{_}She had never seen such emotion in any man's face, and if it was for another, how could she guess it?
10066{_}5232{_}Her blood was singing in her veins, and the old, old question was flying back and forth through her brain like a shuttle through a loom: Which shall it be?
10066{_}5233{_}She called up the picture of Lord Nick, half-broken, but still terrible, she well knew.
10066{_}5234{_}She pitied him, but when did pity wholly rule the heart of a woman?
10066{_}5235{_}And as for Nelly Lebrun, she had the ambition of a young Caesar; she could not fill a second place.

10066{_}5245{_}But now, think quickly.
10066{_}5246{_}For Lord Nick is coming to receive your answer."
10066{_}5247{_}37   If the meeting between Lord Nick and Donnegan earlier that day had wrought up the nerves of The Corner to the point of hysteria; if the singular end of that meeting had piled mystery upon excitement; if the appearance of Donnegan, sitting calmly at the table of the girl who was known to be engaged to Nick, had further stimulated public curiosity, the appearance of Lord Nick was now a crowning burden under which The Corner staggered.
10066{_}5248{_}Yet not a man or a woman stirred from his chair, for everyone knew that if the long-delayed battle between these two gunfighters was at length to take place, neither bullet was apt to fly astray.
10066{_}5249{_}But what happened completed the wreck of The Corner's nerves, for Lord Nick walked quietly across the floor and sat down with Nelly Lebrun and his somber rival.

10066{_}5544{_}"I am, and the point is five thousand dollars that's tied behind the hoss that stands outside your door."

10066{_}5547{_}"Right."

10066{_}5555{_}A wild thought came to the other man.
10066{_}5556{_}Both of Donnegan's hands were far from his weapons.
10066{_}5557{_}Why not a quick draw, a snap shot, and then the glory of having killed this manslayer in single battle for Joe Rix?
10066{_}5558{_}The thought rushed red across his brain and then faded slowly.
10066{_}5559{_}Something kept him back.
10066{_}5560{_}Perhaps it was the singular calm of Donnegan; no matter how quiet he sat he suggested the sleeping cat which can leap out of dead sleep into fighting action at a touch.
10066{_}5561{_}By the time a second thought had come to Joe Rix the idea of an attack was like an idea of suicide.
10066{_}5562{_}"Is that final?"
10066{_}5563{_}he asked, though Donnegan had not said a word.
10066{_}5564{_}"It is."

10066{_}5572{_}We'll put you in his place.

10066{_}5575{_}asked Donnegan.

10066{_}5587{_}But the other continued to smile.
10066{_}5588{_}It gave Joe Rix a shuddering feeling that someone was stealing behind him to block his way to the door.
10066{_}5589{_}He cast one swift glance over his shoulder and then, seeing that the way was clear, he slunk back, always keeping his face to the red-headed man.
10066{_}5590{_}But when he came to the doorway his nerve collapsed.
10066{_}5591{_}He whirled, covered the rest of the distance with a leap, and emerged from the cabin in a fashion ludicrously like one who has been kicked through a door.
10066{_}5592{_}His nerve returned as soon as the sunlight fell warmly upon him again; and he looked around hastily to see if anyone had observed his flight.
10066{_}5593{_}There was no one on the whole hillside except Colonel Macon in the invalid chair, and the colonel was smiling broadly, beneficently.
10066{_}5594{_}He had his perfect hands folded across his breast and seemed to cast a prayer of peace and goodwill upon Joe Rix.
10066{_}5595{_}39   Nelly Lebrun smelled danger.
10066{_}5596{_}She sensed it as plainly as the deer when the puma comes between her and the wind.
10066{_}5597{_}The many tokens that something was wrong came to her by small hints which had to be put together before they assumed any importance.
10066{_}5598{_}First of all, her father, who should have burst out at her in a tirade for having left Lord Nick for Donnegan said nothing at all, but kept a dark smile on his face when she was near him.
10066{_}5599{_}He even insinuated that Nick's time was done and that another was due to supersede him.
10066{_}5600{_}In the second place, she had passed into a room where Masters, Joe Rix, and the Pedlar sat cheek by jowl in close conference with a hum of deep voice.
10066{_}5601{_}But at her appearance all talk was broken off.
10066{_}5602{_}It was not strange that they should not invite her into their confidence if they had some dark work ahead of them; but it was exceedingly suspicious that Joe Rix attempted to pass off their whispers by immediately breaking off the soft talk and springing into the midst of a full-fledged jest; also, it was strangest of all that when the jest ended even the Pedlar, who rarely smiled, now laughed uproariously and smote Joe soundingly upon the back.
10066{_}5603{_}Even a child could have strung these incidents into a chain of evidence which pointed toward danger.
10066{_}5604{_}Obviously the danger was not directly hers, but then it must be directed at some one near to her.
10066{_}5605{_}Her father?
10066{_}5606{_}No, he was more apt to be the mainspring of their action.
10066{_}5607{_}Lord Nick?
10066{_}5608{_}There was nothing to gain by attacking him.
10066{_}5609{_}Who was left?
10066{_}5610{_}Donnegan!
10066{_}5611{_}As the realization came upon her it took her breath away for a moment.
10066{_}5612{_}Donnegan was the man.
10066{_}5613{_}At breakfast everyone had been talking about him.
10066{_}5614{_}Lebrun had remarked that he had a face for the cards--emotionless.
10066{_}5615{_}Joe Rix had commented upon his speed of hand, and the Pedlar had complimented the little man on his dress.
10066{_}5616{_}But at lunch not a word was spoken about Donnegan even after she had dexterously introduced the subject twice.
10066{_}5617{_}Why the sudden silence?
10066{_}5618{_}Between morning and noon Donnegan must have grievously offended them.
10066{_}5619{_}Fear for his sake stimulated her; but above and beyond this, indeed, there was a mighty feminine curiosity.
10066{_}5620{_}She smelled the secret; it reeked through the house, and she was devoured by eagerness to know.
10066{_}5621{_}She handpicked Lord Nick's gang in the hope of finding a weakness among them; some weakness upon which she could play in one of them and draw out what they were all concealing.
10066{_}5622{_}The Pedlar was as unapproachable as a crag on a mountaintop.
10066{_}5623{_}Masters was wise as an outlaw broncho.
10066{_}5624{_}Lester was probably not even in the confidence of the others because since the affair with Landis his nerve had been shattered to bits and the others secretly despised him for being beaten by the youngster at the draw.
10066{_}5625{_}There remained, therefore, only Joe Rix.
10066{_}5626{_}But Joe Rix was a fox of the first quality.
10066{_}5627{_}He lied with the smoothness of silk.
10066{_}5628{_}He could show a dozen colors in as many moments.
10066{_}5629{_}Come to the windward of Joe Rix?
10066{_}5630{_}It was a delicate business!
10066{_}5631{_}But since there was nothing else to do, she fixed her mind upon it, working out this puzzle.
10066{_}5632{_}Joe Rix wished to destroy Donnegan for reasons that were evidently connected with the mines.
10066{_}5633{_}And she must step into his confidence to discover his plans.
10066{_}5634{_}How should it be done?
10066{_}5635{_}And there was a vital need for speed, for they might be within a step of executing whatever mischief it was that they were planning.
10066{_}5636{_}She went down from her room; they were there still, only Joe Rix was not with them.
10066{_}5637{_}She went to the apartment where he and the other three of Nick's gang slept and rapped at the door.
10066{_}5638{_}He maintained his smile when he saw her, but there was an uncertain quiver of his eyebrows that told her much.
10066{_}5639{_}Plainly he was ill at ease.
10066{_}5640{_}Suspicious?
10066{_}5641{_}Ay, there were always clouds of suspicion drifting over the red, round face of Joe Rix.
10066{_}5642{_}She put a tremor of excitement and trouble in her voice.
10066{_}5643{_}"Come into my room, Joe, where we won't be interrupted."
10066{_}5644{_}He followed her without a word, and since she led the way she was able to relax her expression for a necessary moment.
10066{_}5645{_}When she closed the door behind him and faced Joe again she was once more ready to step into her part.
10066{_}5646{_}She did not ask him to sit down.
10066{_}5647{_}She remained for a moment with her hand on the knob and searched the face of Joe Rix eagerly.

10066{_}5656{_}"He's as jealous as the devil, Joe!"
10066{_}5657{_}The fat little man sighed as he looked at her.
10066{_}5658{_}"He can't hear.
10066{_}5659{_}Not through that log wall.
10066{_}5660{_}But we'll talk soft, if you want."
10066{_}5661{_}"Yes, yes.

10066{_}5666{_}The surprising news which the first part of this sentence contained caused Joe to gape, and the girl looked away in concern, enabling him to control his expression.
10066{_}5667{_}For she knew well enough that men hate to appear foolishly surprised.
10066{_}5668{_}And particularly a fox like Joe Rix.

10066{_}5737{_}And if he's gone Nick will come back to me.

10066{_}5800{_}40   The day passed and the night, but how very slowly for Nelly Lebrun; she went up to her room early for she could no longer bear the meaning glances which Joe Rix cast at her from time to time.
10066{_}5801{_}But once in her room it was still harder to bear the suspense as she waited for the noise to die away in the house.
10066{_}5802{_}Midnight, and half an hour more went by, and then, at last, the murmurs and the laughter stopped; she alone was wakeful in Lebrun's.
10066{_}5803{_}And when that time came she caught a scarf around her hair and her shoulders, made of a filmy material which would veil her face but through which she could see, and ventured out of her room and down the hall.
10066{_}5804{_}There was no particular need for such caution, however, it seemed.
10066{_}5805{_}Nothing stirred.
10066{_}5806{_}And presently she was outside the house and hurrying behind the houses and up the hill.
10066{_}5807{_}Still she met nothing.
10066{_}5808{_}If The Corner lived tonight, its life was confined to Milligan's and the gambling house.
10066{_}5809{_}She found Donnegan's shack and the one next to it, which the terrible colonel occupied, entirely dark, but only a moment after she tapped at the door it was opened.
10066{_}5810{_}Donnegan, fully dressed, stood in the entrance, outlined blackly by the light which came faintly from the hooded lantern hanging on the wall.
10066{_}5811{_}Was he sitting up all the night, unable to sleep because he waited breathlessly for that false tryst on the morrow?
10066{_}5812{_}A great tenderness came over the heart of Nelly Lebrun.
10066{_}5813{_}"It is I," she whispered.
10066{_}5814{_}There was a soft exclamation, then she was drawn into the room.

10066{_}5816{_}"Only big George.
10066{_}5817{_}But he's in the kitchen and he won't hear.
10066{_}5818{_}He never hears anything except what's meant for his ear.
10066{_}5819{_}Take this chair!"
10066{_}5820{_}He was putting a blanket over the rough wood to make it more comfortable, and she submitted dumbly to his ministrations.
10066{_}5821{_}It seemed terrible and strange to her that one so gentle should be the object of so much hate--such deadly hate as the members of Nick's gang felt for him.
10066{_}5822{_}And now that he was sitting before her she could see that he had indeed been wakeful for a long time.
10066{_}5823{_}His face was grimly wasted; the lips were compressed as one who has endured long pain; and his eyes gleamed at her out of a profound shadow.
10066{_}5824{_}He remained in the gloom; the light from the lantern fell brightly upon his hands alone--meager, fleshless hands which seemed to represent hardly more strength than that of a child.
10066{_}5825{_}Truly this man was all a creature of spirit and nerve.
10066{_}5826{_}Therein lay his strength, as also his weakness, and again the cherishing instinct grew strong and swept over her.
10066{_}5827{_}"There is no one near," he said, "except the colonel and his daughter.
10066{_}5828{_}They are up the hillside, somewhere.
10066{_}5829{_}Did you see them?"

10066{_}6463{_}How lightly he walked; and he was talking to the calm, pale face which rested in the hollow of his shoulder.
10066{_}6464{_}"He will live?
10066{_}6465{_}He will live?"
10066{_}6466{_}Lou Macon was pleading as she hurried at the side of Lord Nick.
10066{_}6467{_}"God willing, he shall live!"
10066{_}6468{_}It was three hours before Donnegan opened his eyes.
10066{_}6469{_}It was three days before he recovered his senses, and looking aside toward the door he saw a brilliant shaft of sunlight falling into the room.
10066{_}6470{_}In the midst of it sat Lou Macon.
10066{_}6471{_}She had fallen asleep in her great weariness now that the crisis was over.
10066{_}6472{_}Behind her, standing, his great arms folded, stood the indomitable figure of Lord Nick.
10066{_}6473{_}Donnegan saw and wondered greatly.
10066{_}6474{_}Then he closed his eyes dreamily.
10066{_}6475{_}"Hush," said Donnegan to himself, as if afraid that what he saw was all a dream.
10066{_}6476{_}"I'm in heaven, or if I'm not, it's still mighty good to be alive."
